<review>I was pretty excited to hear that Martin's was coming to Los Osos in the place of a restaurant we lost, especially after losing 2 Mexican restaurants in 2 years here.  They did an amazing job renovating the building and adding space, it is a very open and customer friendly space.  Having eaten here twice now I'm pretty happy with this addition to Los Osos.  The pricing is right on par with the other restaurants in town even with the place basically being brand new.  The staff is very friendly and eager to help, understandable since they have been open for a short time.  The food here is quite good as you would come to expect from their restaurant in Cayucos.  The food I've ordered has been cooked quickly and was quality.  The carnitas is great, just a bit crispy on the outside and so flavorful and moist once you get into it.  Their chili verde is great, especially with the tomatillo salsa.  It has a nice little citrusy kick to it.  I'm stoked to have another restaurant here, especially one with history in the county.  My only complaint is no Italian food, I was really looking forward to having the Italian dishes here as we don't have any Italian in Los Osos anymore.  Martin's has great people, great food, good lunch specials, and is a great addition to Los Osos.< /review>< gmapID>

<rating>2<//rating>< review>
I may have been expecting too much.  The staff was VERY friendly and the information provided by Dr. Dougherty was very professional and thorough.  Perhaps that is all I should have wanted.   However,  since eyesight is the most important of my senses I was hoping for a bit of genuine appreciation of the individual patient.   I hasten to add I was NOT looking for a new best friend.   I did hope that in our brief interaction I could begin to feel a level of comfort similar to that I have had with my personal physicians. DLV is a well oiled machine and clearly the overall goal is to complete as many surgeries as possible with professionalism and positive outcomes.  The discomfort comes from the assembly line process starting at the front desk and moving, ultimately to the "counselor" who  discusses costs and financing.  There is very clear and persistent pressure to choose a package and most importantly SET a surgical date.  The further along the assembly line I progressed the more apparent it was that I needed to choose that date.  I have no problem with the corporate goal of maximizing surgeries and  profits but it simply should not be as apparent to a new patient.<//review>

<date>1610009622865<//date><Review>Much gratitude and appreciation to Dr. Paul Dougherty and his compassionate staff for leveling up my Real World Avatar!

Ever since 5th grade, I was wearing either contacts or glasses just to simply see. Given all the events happening in 2020 and predictions of zombies in 2021 by Nostrodamus:

"Few young people: halfdead to give a start. Dead through spite, he will cause the others to shine. And in an exalted place some great evils to occur: Sad concepts will come to harm each one, Temporal dignified, the Mass to succeed. Fathers and mothers dead of infinite sorrows, Women in mourning, the pestilent she monster: The Great One to be no more, all the world to end."

It's good to know this is one less thing I have to worry about while having to sprint out of my house at a moment's notice. The assurance of being able to run away from future zombies without having to secure a month's supply of my Acuvue contacts is a super life-saving investment.

If the astrologers are right, I would keenly look into fixing your eyes before you too are in the need. Realistically, the "half-dead to start" might be referring to all the people locked away at home blindly consuming content from their screens. Who knows, better to hedge your bets before you can't determine if that person in front of you is coming up to you for a hug or to nom on your grey matter.

For this matter, I highly recommend Dr. Paul Dougherty for his professionalism and his ability to give you the emotional reassurance that your eyes will be taken care of. His staff was super informative and expressed great empathy to me that I felt so at ease on surgery day. The other vision centers I checked out didn't have as nice of facilities or as many options. Due to my eyes being -8.00, I had the option of either Lasik or PRK...until I stepped into Dougherty's office, I had no idea there was a new treatment called ICL. ICL consists of them putting in contacts into your eyes. It's reversible, doesn't cause dry eyes (my eyes are already dry), and has natural UV protection. :)

So thank you Dr. Paul Dougherty for giving me a chance on surviving a predicted zombies uprising this year. I had -8.00 vision so just being able to see so clearly after a short nap from surgery made me bursting with gratitude and appreciation. Being able to swim in the ocean and open my eyes to the fishes and any possible incoming water zombies was also a superpower I didn't have before.

Sending much love to a zombie-less 2021 year.< /Review><user_name>Swan<//user_name><rate>5< /rate>< Gmap_id>

<Text>My procedure was for RPK surgery, which took place on July 22, 2019. From my initial setting up of an appointment to having the actual surgery performed and the end result was extremely UNSATISFACTORY:
A.) I met with my referring cataract surgery physician, Dr Abroms on July 15, 2019 to discuss RPK surgery y Dr Dougherty. Other than setting up the approximate appointment time for my surgery with Dr Dougherty, no details were discussed regarding the RPK procedure as far as risks or possible complications. I was not given any information regarding risks and complications of the surgery. I assumed that that information would be provided by Dr. Dougherty's office and that I would have an opportunity to discuss the procedure with him.
B.) I was told that I would receive a phone call from Dr. Dougherty's office on Friday, July 19, 2019 to set up the actual time of the RPK surgery. By 3:00 PM on that Friday, I had not received a phone call, so I called them. The phone was answered by a recording saying that the office was closed for "Professional Development Training". I left my name and phone number in order to receive a return call.
C). Emma Caldron called me about 15 minutes later. I was given the time for the scheduled procedure, papers were faxed to me explaining risks and possible complications, which I was to sign and return. By the time I finished reading and signing some all the forms, it was 4:30 PM- too late to discuss my questions and concerns with anyone. I did not sign some of the papers because I would have been agreeing to having discussed the procedure and discussed my concerns, which, of course, I had not.
D). I finally talked to Dr Dougherty the morning of the surgery and signed the papers agreeing to the fact that I had discussed the procedure, but at this point we were within an hour of the procedure. I should have cancelled the whole thing because I just did not feel as though I had had enough time to think about the risks and complications and to ask pertinent questions.
E.) As it turns out, I experienced very significant complications and I am still under the care of a retina specialist and my vision is compromised. So, I gave the this review a 'One Star' because that is the lowest rating possible.
F.) One caveat: the staff at the facility were all very friendly and pleasant to deal with.<//Text>< Gmap_id>

<Pictures>None< /Pictures>< Review>
This is not your typical restaurant experience. Just with that it deserves a visit. The food is good, sometimes very good, but not spectacular. The Basque setup include bread, soup (our was a very bland chicken noodle), green salad (simple and excellent vinaigrette), macaroni salad (simple and excellent), veggie (eh), and varying sides (I had a so-so paella), ice cream (hey, they never brought me my ice cream!).

Entrees are good. At our table we had a surprisingly good calamari steak sandwich, a good lamb steak and a good enough roast chicken half.

Friendly unpretentious service, good home-style food. Enjoy!</Review>

<userid>101809630506525731506< /userid><Rate>5< /Rate><Name>Brandy Herrera</Name><date>1495909969944< /date>< text>
Food taste amazing! Always great service!<//text>
<Resp>None< /Resp><gmap_id>0x80945e1f54e8ebbd:0x35202c0b276c3edc</gmap_id><pics>None<//pics></record></dataset><record>
< review>
Basque Food????? Last Saturday we were in Fresno for my birthday and decided to have Basque cuisine.. My wife and I have been enjoying Basque style dining for 30 or so years and were extremely disappointed. About the only thing Basque about it was family style dining and purchasing pickled tongue which is normally served with the meal. We have had Basque food in several cities since the Basque restaurant closed in Santa Maria 30 or more years ago and all were primarily the same with slight variations. The soup for the evening which was a Saturday night was clam chowder .  It wasn't even Friday night. Minnestroni soup with beans and  salsa is the normal soup. The "stew"  which we were hoping would be Basque style Minnestroni and as described was Chile Verde with pinto beans (where's the pasta?)The dinner is normally served with a side of pasta which we know is traditional. Never dining in maybe 20 or so Basque restaurants have we been served either of these items. We did order the pickled tongue which is normally served as a side. So basically we ate what ever they had available but Basque NOOOO. For desert the meal came with ice cream. You had your choice of vanilla or nothing. Spamoni ? Every Basque restaurant has Spamoni ice cream with options. So, I am sorry but there was nothing about the food that was Basque and what was served was just weird if you wanted Basque cuisine. The bread tasted old and we ordered a margarita and a bloody mary with salt. They must have been out of salt. The rest of food was actually very good. My rib eye was delicious. My wife's lamb steak was also although she had a slight problem finding any meat among the bone.  It was sort of like going to a hamburger restaurant ordering a hamburger and being served a hot dog. Even though you may have enjoyed the hot dog it just isn't a hamburger. $85 for basically some sort of mismatch food. Basque no way. The 3 star rating was based only on the fact that what we were served was actually good.</review>

<username>Hungry Chola<//username>< time>
1423941498956<//time>
<rate>4<//rate><Text>J&S is one of two food stands that serve quintessential comfort Chicano food.

Chicano food (by my definition) is an oft-overlooked hybrid of Mexican and American casual cuisine. It particularly shines in terms of burger-stand fare.

J&S, along with Lupe's #2, is one of the few competent vestiges of Chicano food that captured the food of East LA in the sixties and seventies.
I don't know how this turned into a history lesson.

The food is good. It was probably better 20 years ago or more. Ask people of a certain age with no homegrown connection and they'll tell you the same thing. Ask people who've eaten there regularly their entire lives and they'll deny anything has changed. The changes have been gradual; noticed only by those return occasionally.

The Soft Tostada is a perfect example. Once an amazing  combination of perfectly cooked beans mixed with taqueria-style guacamole, lettuce, tomatoes and cheese encased in a glorious tortilla is now but a slightly limp version of its former glory.

Like a fading movie star: It's still good. It still gets the job done. It's cheap and it's open 24 hours.

I think the simile stopped working about halfway (or did it?).</Text>< Pics>
None</Pics>
